widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="font-weight: 500; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(0, 0, 0, 0); -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;"><div><b>Internet of things opportunities.</b></div><div>Python may become popular for the Internet of things, as new platforms such as Raspberry Pi are based on it, Carbonnelle says. Raspberry Pi's documentation cites the language as &quot;a wonderful and powerful programming language that's easy to use (easy to read and write) and with Raspberry Pi lets you connect your project to the real world.&quot;</div></div><div><br/></div></div></div><hr/><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>That's a pretty broad question. A more relevant question might be, Why is Python good for x? However, I'll do my best here.</b></div><div><br/></div><div>As far as &quot;very high level&quot; interpreted languages go, Python is on-par with PHP, Ruby, Perl, etc. in term of performance and capabilities. In my experience, the big win for Python is code readability. Since the syntax is so strict, certain stylistic practices are encouraged (i.e. easy to do) and others are discouraged (i.e. hard to do). This leads to very consistent code across different projects and programmers. As a result, when Python projects scale, it is easy for many developers to get in the mix without huge managerial overhead.</div><div><br/></div><div>A second reason is popularity. There are certain circles that prefer Python for one reason or another. In the math community for example, there is quite a lot of existing code that can be leveraged. Also, Google has developed several open source projects in Python. So if you want to use them, learning Python is a good idea.</div><div><br/></div><div>And finally there's the issue of preference. Some people simply like the &quot;Pythonic&quot; way of doing things and the language makes sense to them.</div><div><br/></div><div>I write Python, Ruby and PHP regularly and in the end they all get the job done.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="font-weight: 500; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(0, 0, 0, 0); -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;"><div><b>Some of the most important reasons to learn C++ are:</b></div></div><ul><li>Understanding memory management and pointer usage.</li><li>Inventing your own class hierarchy instead of relying on pre-packaged libraries from your language vendor.</li><li>Learning how to use templates and generic programming principles.</li></ul><div><br/></div></div></div><hr/><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;"><div>In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computing" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Computing">computing</a>, <b>ANSI escape codes</b> (or <b>escape sequences</b>) are a method using <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-band_signaling" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="In-band signaling">in-band signaling</a> to control the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formatted_text" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Formatted text">formatting, color, and other output options</a> on video <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Text_terminal" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Text terminal">text terminals</a>. To encode this formatting information, certain sequences of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byte" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Byte">bytes</a> are embedded into the text, which the terminal looks for and interprets as commands, not as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_encoding" style="text-decoration: underline; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Character encoding">character codes</a>.</div></div><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;">ANSI codes were introduced in the 1970s and became widespread in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minicomputer" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Minicomputer">minicomputer</a>/<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainframe_computer" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Mainframe computer">mainframe</a> market by the early 1980s. They were used by the nascent <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulletin_board_system" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Bulletin board system">bulletin board system</a> market to offer improved displays compared to earlier systems lacking cursor movement, leading to even more widespread use.</span></span></span></div><div><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><br/></span></span></span></div><div style="margin: 0px 0px 5px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; width: 660px; word-wrap: break-word; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both;"><div><span style="font-family: Arial, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, sans-serif;"><b><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX" rel="nofollow noreferrer" style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-size: 15px; color: rgb(0, 89, 153); text-decoration: none; cursor: pointer;">POSIX</a></b><span style="font-size: 15px;"><b><span style="color: rgb(36, 39, 41);"> is a family of standards, specified by the </span><a href="http://www.ieee.org/portal/site" rel="nofollow noreferrer" style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-size: 15px; color: rgb(0, 89, 153); text-decoration: none; cursor: pointer;">IEEE</a></b><span style="color: rgb(36, 39, 41);"><b>,</b> to clarify and make uniform the application programming interfaces (and ancillary issues, such as commandline shell utilities) provided by Unix-y operating systems. When you write your programs to rely on POSIX standards, you can be pretty sure to be able to port them easily among a large family of Unix derivatives (including Linux, but not limited to it!); if and when you use some Linux API that's not standardized as part of Posix, you will have a harder time if and when you want to port that program or library to other Unix-y systems (e.g., MacOSX) in the future.</span></span></span></div></div></div></div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>Type inference</b></div><div>refers to the automatic deduction of the data type of an expression in a programming language. If some, but not all, type annotations are already present, it is termed type reconstruction. </div><div>It is a feature present in some strongly statically typed languages. It is often characteristic of functional programming languages in general. The ability to infer types automatically makes many programming tasks easier, leaving the programmer free to omit type annotations while still permitting type checking.</div><div><br/></div><div><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>strongly typed or weakly typed (loosely typed)</b>.</div><div>These terms do not have a precise definition, but in general, a strongly typed language is more likely to generate an error or refuse to compile if the argument passed to a function does not closely match the expected type. On the other hand, a very weakly typed language may produce unpredictable results or may perform implicit type conversion.[1] A different but related concept is latent typing.</div></div><p style="margin: 0.5em 0px; color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"></p></div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>functional programming</b></div><div>is a programming paradigm—a style of building the structure and elements of computer programs—that treats computation as the evaluation of mathematical functions and avoids changing-state and mutable data. It is a declarative programming paradigm, which means programming is done with expressions[1] or declarations[2] instead of statements. In functional code, the output value of a function depends only on the arguments that are input to the function, so calling a function f twice with the same value for an argument x will produce the same result f(x) each time. Eliminating side effects, i.e. changes in state that do not depend on the function inputs, can make it much easier to understand and predict the behavior of a program, which is one of the key motivations for the development of functional programming.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>a mutator method</b> is a method used to control changes to a variable. They are also widely known as <b>setter methods.</b> Often a setter is accompanied by a <b>getter medhod (also known as an accessor),</b> which returns the value of the private member variable.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF)</b></div><div>is a type of attack that occurs when a malicious web site, email, blog, instant message, or program causes a user's web browser to perform an unwanted action on a trusted site for which the user is currently authenticated.Nov 1, 2016</div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Bread - analogous to CRUD</b></div><div>(Browse, Read, Edit, Add, Delete)</div><div><br/></div><div><b>A Yellow Screen of Death</b></div><div>(also called YSoD) occurs when an <a dir="ltr" href="http://asp.net/">ASP.NET</a> web application encounters a problem and crashes. It also appears on the browser Mozilla Firefox when there are errors in reading the .xml web format.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>pointer</b></div><div>In computer science, a pointer is a programming language object, whose value refers to (or &quot;points to&quot;) another value stored elsewhere in the computer memory using its memory address. A pointer references a location in memory, and obtaining the value stored at that location is known as dereferencing the pointer. As an analogy, a page number in a book's index could be considered a pointer to the corresponding page; dereferencing such a pointer would be done by flipping to the page with the given page number.</div><div><br/></div><div>Pointers to data significantly improve performance for repetitive operations such as traversing strings, lookup tables, control tables and tree structures. In particular, it is often much cheaper in time and space to copy and dereference pointers than it is to copy and access the data to which the pointers point.</div><div><b><br/></b></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>Big O Notation</b></div><div>Big O notation is a mathematical notation that describes the limiting behavior of a function when the argument tends towards a particular value or infinity. It is a member of a family of notations invented by Paul Bachmann, Edmund Landau, and others, collectively called Bachmann–Landau notation or asymptotic notation.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">Long short-term memory</b><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> (</span><b style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">LSTM</b><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">)</span></div><div><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">i</span><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">s a </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Recurrent neural network"><b>recurrent neural network</b></a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"><b> (RNN)</b> architecture (<b>an </b></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_neural_network" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Artificial neural network"><b>artificial neural network</b></a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">) proposed in 1997 by </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepp_Hochreiter" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Sepp Hochreiter">Sepp Hochreiter</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> and </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Schmidhuber" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Jürgen Schmidhuber">Jürgen Schmidhuber</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">.</span><sup style="unicode-bidi: isolate; white-space: nowrap; font-size: 11.2px; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal; color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_short-term_memory#cite_note-lstm1997-2" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none; white-space: nowrap;">[2]</a></sup><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> Like most RNNs, an LSTM network is </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_completeness" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Turing completeness">universal</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> in the sense that given enough network units it can compute anything a conventional computer can compute, provided it has the proper </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weight" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Weight">weight</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matrix_(mathematics)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Matrix (mathematics)">matrix</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">, which may be viewed as its program. Unlike traditional RNNs, an LSTM network is well-suited to learn from experience to </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classification_in_machine_learning" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Classification in machine learning">classify</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">, </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_data_processing" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Computer data processing">process</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> and </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predict" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Predict">predict</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_series" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Time series">time series</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> when there are very long time lags of unknown size between important events. This is one of the main reasons why LSTM outperforms alternative RNNs and </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hidden_Markov_models" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px;" title="Hidden Markov models">hidden Markov models</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> and other sequence learning methods in numerous applications.</span></div><div><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><br/></span></span></span></span></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>A database is an array of arrays.</b></div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><strong style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-variant-numeric: inherit; font-weight: bold; font-stretch: inherit; font-family: &quot;Open Sans&quot;, &quot;Helvetica Neue&quot;, Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; font-size: 14.5px; vertical-align: baseline; color: rgb(85, 85, 85); letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">Behavior-Driven Development (BDD)</strong></div><div><span style="color: rgb(85, 85, 85); font-family: &quot;Open Sans&quot;, &quot;Helvetica Neue&quot;, Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; font-size: 14.5px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">combines the general techniques and principles of TDD with ideas from domain-driven design. BDD is a design activity where you build pieces of functionality incrementally guided by the expected behavior. </span></div><div><b><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif;"><span style="background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><span style="color: rgb(85, 85, 85);"><br/></span></span></span></b></div><div><strong style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: bold; font-stretch: inherit; font-family: 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: rgb(85, 85, 85); letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">ATDD</strong><span style="color: rgb(85, 85, 85); font-family: 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;"> stands for </span><strong style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: bold; font-stretch: inherit; font-family: 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; vertical-align: baseline; color: rgb(85, 85, 85); letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">Acceptance Test Driven Development</strong><span style="color: rgb(85, 85, 85); font-family: 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">,</span></div><div><span style="color: rgb(85, 85, 85); font-family: 'Open Sans', 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, freesans, clean, sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">it is also less commonly designated as Storytest Driven Development (STDD). It is a technique used to bring customers into the test design process before coding has begun. It is a collaborative practice where users, testers, and developers define automated acceptance criteria. ATDD helps to ensure that all project members understand precisely what needs to be done and implemented. </span></div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Test-driven development (TDD)</b></div><div>is a technique of using automated unit tests to drive the design of software and force decoupling of dependencies. The result of using this practice is a comprehensive suite of unit tests that can be run at any time to provide feedback that the software is still working.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Polymorphism</b></div><div>In programming languages and type theory, <b>polymorphism</b> (from Greek πολύς, polys, &quot;many, much&quot; and μορφή, morphē, &quot;form, shape&quot;) is the provision of a single interface to entities of different types.[1] A polymorphic type is one whose operations can also be applied to values of some other type, or types.\</div></div><div><b><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><br/></span></span></span></span></b></div><div><b style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">lexical scope</b><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">,</span></div><div><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">a name always refers to its (more or less) local lexical environment. This is a property of the program text and is made independent of the runtime </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Call_stack" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="Call stack">call stack</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;"> by the language implementation. Because this matching only requires analysis of the static program text, this type of scoping is also called </span><b style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">static scoping</b><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">. Lexical scoping is standard in all </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ALGOL" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="ALGOL">ALGOL</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">-based languages such as </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(programming_language)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="Pascal (programming language)">Pascal</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">, </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modula2" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="Modula2">Modula2</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;"> and </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ada_(programming_language)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="Ada (programming language)">Ada</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;"> as well as in modern functional languages such as </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ML_(programming_language)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="ML (programming language)">ML</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;"> and </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haskell_(programming_language)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background-image: none; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-position: initial initial; background-repeat: initial initial;" title="Haskell (programming language)">Haskell</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); float: none; display: inline !important;">.</span></div><div><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><br/></span></span></span></span></div><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><b>closures</b></span></span></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);">(also <b>lexical closures</b> or <b>function closures</b>) are techniques for implementing </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lexically_scoped" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Lexically scoped">lexically scoped</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"> </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_binding" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Name binding">name binding</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"> in languages with </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First-class_function" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="First-class function">first-class functions</a></span></span><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 14px;">.A closure—unlike a plain function—allows the function to access those <i>captured variables</i> through the closure's copies of their values or references, even when the function is invoked outside their scope.</span></span></span></div></div><div><b><br/></b></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div><b>Ternary Operator</b></div><div>var headline = ( &lt;h1&gt; {age &gt;= drinkingAge ? 'Buy Drink' : 'Do Teen Stuff' } &lt;/h1&gt; );</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div><b>The Elastic Stack</b></div><div><br/></div><div><i><b>Kibana</b></i></div><div>Visualize your data. Navigate the Elastic Stack.Kibana gives shape to your data and is the extensible user interface for configuring and managing all aspects of the Elastic Stack.</div><div><i><b>Elasticsearch</b></i></div><div>Search, analyze, and store your data. Elasticsearch is a distributed, JSON-based search and analytics engine designed for horizontal scalability, maximum reliability, and easy management.</div><div><i><b>Beats</b></i></div><div>Beats is a platform for lightweight shippers that send data from edge machines to Logstash and Elasticsearch.</div><div><i><b>Logstash</b></i></div><div>Logstash is a dynamic data collection pipeline with an extensible plugin ecosystem and strong Elasticsearch synergy.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="clear: none; padding-top: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div><b>A MapReduce</b></div><div>job usually splits the input data-set into independent chunks which are processed by the map tasks in a completely parallel manner. The framework sorts the outputs of the maps, which are then input to the reduce tasks. Typically both the input and the output of the job are stored in a file-system.Aug 4, 2013</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Apache Hadoop™</b></div><div>was born out of a need to process an avalanche of big data. The web was generating more and more information on a daily basis, and it was becoming very difficult to index over one billion pages of content. In order to cope, Google invented a new style of data processing known as MapReduce. A year after Google published a white paper describing the MapReduce framework, Doug Cutting and Mike Cafarella, inspired by the white paper, created Hadoop to apply these concepts to an open-source software framework to support distribution for the Nutch search engine project. Given the original case, Hadoop was designed with a simple write-once storage infrastructure.</div></div></div><div style="text-align: left; margin: 0px; clear: both; padding-bottom: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="position: relative; clear: both; padding-bottom: 0px;"><div><b>ETL (Extract, Transform and Load)</b></div><div>is a process in data warehousing responsible for pulling data out of the source systems and placing it into a data warehouse.</div><div><br/></div><div><b><br/></b></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="text-align: left; margin: 0px; clear: both; padding-bottom: 16px; padding-left: 16px; padding-right: 16px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="position: relative; clear: both; padding-bottom: 0px;"><div><b>A NoSQL</b></div><div>(often interpreted as Not only SQL) database provides a mechanism for storage and retrieval of data that is modeled in means other than the tabular relations used in relational databases. Motivations for this approach include simplicity of design, horizontal scaling, and finer control over availability.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>MongoDB is</b></div><div>an open source, document-oriented database designed with both scalability and developer agility in mind. Instead of storing your data in tables and rows as you would with a relational database, in MongoDB you store JSON-like documents with dynamic schemas.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Cassandra</b> -</div><div>Introduction. Apache Cassandra is a highly scalable, high-performance distributed database designed to handle large amounts of data across many commodity servers, providing high availability with no single point of failure. It is a type of NoSQL database.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Apache CouchDB</b></div><div>is open source database software that focuses on ease of use and having an architecture that &quot;completely embraces the Web&quot;.[2] It has a document-oriented NoSQL database architecture and is implemented in the concurrency-oriented language Erlang; it uses JSON to store data, JavaScript as its query language using MapReduce, and HTTP for an API.[2]</div><div><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><table border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="margin: 0px 0px 1.71429rem; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><br/></div><div><b>Perl</b></div><div>is a script programming language that is similar in syntax to the C language and that includes a number of popular UNIX facilities such as sed, awk, and tr. Perl is an interpreted language that can optionally be compiled just before execution into either C code or cross-platform bytecode.</div><div>Software developers call Perl the &quot;Duct Tape of the Internet&quot; because the programming language lends itself to quick, easy fixes of data problems. </div><div>Perl is a high-level programming language that excels at sophisticated text file processing and, among other uses, can generate Hyper Text Markup Language output for Web pages. It includes interfaces to incorporate databases, making<br/></div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Cygwin is:</b></div><ul><li>a large collection of GNU and Open Source tools which provide functionality similar to a Linux distribution on Windows.</li><li>a DLL (cygwin1.dll) which provides substantial POSIX API functionality</li></ul><div><i>Cygwin is not:</i></div><ul><li>a way to run native Linux apps on Windows. You must rebuild your application from source if you want it to run on Windows.</li><li>a way to magically make native Windows apps aware of UNIX® functionality like signals, ptys, etc. Again, you need to build your apps from source if you want to take advantage of Cygwin functionality.</li></ul><div><br/></div><div><b style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">tmux</b></div><div>is a software application that can be used to multiplex several virtual consoles, allowing a user to access multiple separate terminal sessions inside a single terminal window or remote terminal session. It is useful for dealing with multiple programs from a command-line interface, and for separating programs from the Unix shell that started the program.[2] It provides much of the same functionality as GNU Screen, but it is distributed under a BSD license.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>GNU Screen</b></div><div>is a terminal multiplexer, a software application that can be used to multiplex several virtual consoles, allowing a user to access multiple separate login sessions inside a single terminal window, or detach and reattach sessions from a terminal. It is useful for dealing with multiple programs from a command line interface, and for separating programs from the session of the Unix shell that started the program, particularly so a remote process continues running even when the user is disconnected.</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 5px; Mobile apps with HTML, CSS &amp; JS, Target multiple platforms with one code base, Free and open source</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>Perf Tools</b></div><div>A miscellaneous collection of in-development and unsupported performance analysis tools for Linux ftrace and perf_events (aka the &quot;perf&quot; command). Both ftrace and perf are core Linux tracing tools, included in the kernel source. ... These are intended for Linux 3.2 and newer kernels.</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-style: normal; font-stretch: inherit; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>TDD, QA Positions are easier to get... interested?</b></div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>RSpec</b></div><div>Behaviour Driven Development for Ruby. Making TDD Productive and Fun.</div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Cucumber</b></div><div style="box-sizing: border-box; margin: 0px 0px 26px; font-weight: 300;"><div>At a glance, Cucumber might just look like another tool for running automated tests. But it’s more than that.</div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b><br/></b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b>QUnit</b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">is a powerful, easy-to-use JavaScript unit testing framework. It's used by the jQuery, jQuery UI and jQuery Mobile projects and is capable of testing any generic JavaScript code, including itself!</div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><br/></div><div><b>test-unit (Test::Unit)</b> is unit testing framework for Ruby, based on xUnit principles. These were originally designed by Kent Beck, creator of extreme programming software development methodology, for Smalltalk's SUnit. It allows writing tests, checking results and automated testing in Ruby.</div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Capybara</b></div><div>Tired of clicking around in your browser trying to make sure your applications work as expected? Capybara is a library written in the Rubyprogramming language which makes it easy to simulate how a user interacts with your application. Capybara can talk with many different drivers which execute your tests through the same clean and simple interface. You can seamlessly choose between Selenium, Webkit or pure Ruby drivers.</div><div>Tackle the asynchronous web with Capybara's powerful synchronization features. Capybara automatically waits for your content to appear on the page, you never have to issue any manual sleeps.</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both;"><div style="clear: none; padding: 10px 16px; font-style: normal; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="box-sizing: border-box; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>Optimizing CSS and JS for production</b></div><div>Developers have two tasks to perform when we try to optimize CSS and JavaScript files for production: minification and concatenation.</div><div><br/></div><div>One problem developers face when automating this process is that it's difficult to concatenate your scripts in the correct order.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-style: normal; font-stretch: inherit; vertical-align: baseline; word-break: break-word; box-sizing: border-box; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="overflow: hidden; padding-bottom: 20px;"><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="box-sizing: border-box; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>Globbing (Regular Expressions for Filenames)</b></div><div>*.scss: The * pattern is a wildcard that matches any pattern in the current directory. In this case, we’re matching any files ending with .scss in the root folder (project).</div><div><br/></div><div>**/*.scss: This is a more extreme version of the *pattern that matches any file ending with .scss in the root folder and any child directories.</div><div><br/></div><div>!not-me.scss: The ! indicates that Gulp should exclude the pattern from its matches, which is useful if you had to exclude a file from a matched pattern. In this case, not-me.scss would be excluded from the match.</div><div><br/></div><div>*.+(scss|sass): The plus + and parentheses ()allows Gulp to match multiple patterns, with different patterns separated by the pipe | character. In this case, Gulp will match any file ending with .scss or .sass in the root folder.</div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 5px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; width: 660px; word-wrap: break-word; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div><b>USE WEBPACK 2</b></div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Synchronous Javascript</b></div><div>Javascript is always synchronous and single-threaded meaning if you're executing aJavascript block of code on a page then no other Javascript on that page will currently be executed. Javascript is only asynchronous in the sense that it can make, for example, AJAX calls.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Asynchronous Javascript</b></div><div>The result of the query will then be stored by the &quot;callback&quot; function sometime afterwards. The main difference is with asynchronous programming, you don't stop execution otherwise. You can continue executing other code while the 'request' is being made.</div><div><br/></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b>Try, Catch </b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">The try block contains code that may provoke an error, while the catch block contains the code that handles some or all errors. If an error occurs in the try block, program control is passed to the catch block. The value of exception is the value of the error that occurred in the try block.</div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><br/></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">try {</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">    Block of code to try</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">}</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">catch(err) {</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">    Block of code to handle errors</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">}</div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><br/></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; font-style: normal; font-stretch: inherit; vertical-align: baseline; word-break: break-word; box-sizing: border-box; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 5px; padding: 0px; border: 0px; width: 660px; word-wrap: break-word; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="margin: 0px 0px 1em; padding: 0px; border: 0px; clear: both;"><div style="clear: none; padding: 10px 16px; font-style: normal; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="box-sizing: border-box; font-style: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b>PHP Methods/Functions used in REST API CRUD</b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- PDOStatement::bindParam ( mixed $parameter , mixed $variable )<br/></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- final public mixed SolrParams::getParam ([ string $param_name ] )<br/></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- DOMElement::getAttribute() - Returns value of attribute</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- DOMElement::hasAttribute() - Checks to see if attribute exists</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- DOMElement::setAttribute() - Adds new attribute</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- DOMElement::removeAttribute() - Removes attribute</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- Exception::getMessage ( void )</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- PDOStatement::execute ([ array $input_parameters ] )</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">- PDOStatement::fetch()<br/></div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><br/></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><hr/><div style="margin: 0px 0px 0.7em; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b>PHP Data Objects= PDO</b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><br/></div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b>object-&gt;method in PHP is same as object.method or object.property</b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><span style="color: rgb(36, 39, 41);"><span style="font-size: 15px;"><span style="font-family: Arial, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, sans-serif;">The object operator, “-&gt;”, is used in object scope to access methods and properties of an object. It’s meaning is to say that what is on the right of the operator is a member of the object instantiated into the variable on the left side of the operator. Instantiated is the key term here.</span></span></span></div></div><div style="font-weight: normal;"><b>Scope Resolution Operator (::) </b></div><div style="font-weight: normal;">The Scope Resolution Operator (also called Paamayim Nekudotayim) or in simpler terms, the double colon, is a token that allows access tostatic, constant, and overridden properties or methods of a class.</div><div style="font-weight: normal;">Example:  <span style="font-family: &quot;Fira Mono&quot;, &quot;Source Code Pro&quot;, monospace;
