border: 0px; margin: 0px; text-align: left; color: rgb(33, 33, 33); padding: 7px 8px 8px; background: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.952941); vertical-align: top;">User loads the page and starts interacting (for example, scrolls or opens navigation).</td></tr></tbody></table><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Image [11].png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div>From a purely mathematical point of view, every frame has a budget of 16.66ms (divide 1 second by 60) but, because browsers have housekeeping to do, the reality is that there is a window of 10ms for your code during animations.</div><div><br/></div><div>In high pressure points like animations, the key is to do nothing where you can, and where you can’t, do the absolute minimum. Whenever possible, make use of the 100ms response to pre-calculate expensive work so that you maximize your chances of hitting 60fps.</div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>A web worker (JS)</b></div><div>is a JavaScript that runs in the background, independently of other scripts, without affecting the performance of the page. You can continue to do whatever you want: clicking, selecting things, etc., while the web worker runs in the background.</div><div><b><br/></b></div><hr/><div><b>Object-relational mapping</b></div><div>(ORM, O/RM, and O/R mapping tool) in computer science is a programming technique for converting data between incompatible type systems in object-oriented programming languages. This creates, in effect, a &quot;virtual object database&quot; that can be used from within the programming language.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Hibernate ORM (Hibernate in short)</b></div><div>is an object-relational mapping framework for the Java language. It provides a framework for mapping an object-oriented domain model to a relational database.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Entity Framework (EF)</b></div><div>is an open source object-relational mapping (ORM) framework for <a dir="ltr" href="http://ado.net/">ADO.NET</a>, part of .NET Framework.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>SQLAlchemy</b></div><div>is an open source SQL toolkit and object-relational mapper (ORM) for the Python programming language released under the MIT License.</div><div><b><br/></b></div><hr/><div><b>Virtualization:</b></div><div>Linux virtual machines on a Windows host or vice versa. static amount of resources (CPU, RAM, storage), hypervisor will eat up a lot of resources (this is usually referred to as overhead)</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Containerisation</b></div><div>Containerization allows multiple applications to run in isolated partitions of a single Linux kernel. Linux cgroups and namespaces are the underlying Linux kernel technologies used to isolate, secure and manage the containers. Higher performance (closer to bare metal). Elastic resource allocation. Linux only (single kernel)</div><hr/><div><b>Code smell</b></div><div>Also known as bad smell, in computer programming code, refers to any symptom in the source code of a program that possibly indicates a deeper problem. According to Martin Fowler, &quot;a code smell is a surface indication that usually corresponds to a deeper problem in the system&quot;.</div><div><br/></div><ul><li><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="font-size: 14px;"><b>Application-level smells</b>:</span></span></span><ul style="list-style-type: disc; margin: 0.3em 0px 0px 1.6em; padding: 0px; list-style-image: url(&quot;data:image/svg+xml,%3C%3Fxml%20version%3D%221.0%22%20encoding%3D%22UTF-8%22%3F%3E%0A%3Csvg%20xmlns%3D%22http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2F2000%2Fsvg%22%20version%3D%221.1%22%20width%3D%225%22%20height%3D%2213%22%3E%0A%3Ccircle%20cx%3D%222.5%22%20cy%3D%229.5%22%20r%3D%222.5%22%20fill%3D%22%2300528c%22%2F%3E%0A%3C%2Fsvg%3E%0A&quot;); color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><li><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><span style="font-size: 14px;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duplicate_code" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Duplicate code">Duplicated code</a></i>: identical or very similar code exists in more than one location.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><i>Contrived complexity</i>: forced usage of overcomplicated <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design_pattern_(computer_science)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Design pattern (computer science)">design patterns</a> where simpler design would suffice.</li></ul></li><li><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><b>Class-level smells</b>:</div><ul style="list-style-type: disc; margin: 0.3em 0px 0px 1.6em; padding: 0px; list-style-image: url(&quot;data:image/svg+xml,%3C%3Fxml%20version%3D%221.0%22%20encoding%3D%22UTF-8%22%3F%3E%0A%3Csvg%20xmlns%3D%22http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2F2000%2Fsvg%22%20version%3D%221.1%22%20width%3D%225%22%20height%3D%2213%22%3E%0A%3Ccircle%20cx%3D%222.5%22%20cy%3D%229.5%22%20r%3D%222.5%22%20fill%3D%22%2300528c%22%2F%3E%0A%3C%2Fsvg%3E%0A&quot;); color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Large class</i></b>: a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Class (computer science)">class</a> that has grown too large. See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/God_object" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="God object">God object</a>.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Feature envy</i></b>: a class that uses methods of another class excessively.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Inappropriate intimacy</i></b>: a class that has dependencies on implementation details of another class.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Refused bequest</i></b>: a class that <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_overriding_(programming)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Method overriding (programming)">overrides</a> a method of a base class in such a way that the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contract_(software)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Contract (software)">contract</a> of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base_class" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Base class">base class</a> is not honored by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derived_class" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Derived class">derived class</a>. See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liskov_substitution_principle" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Liskov substitution principle">Liskov substitution principle</a>.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Lazy class / freeloader</i></b>: a class that does too little.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Excessive use of literals</i></b>: these should be coded as named constants, to improve readability and to avoid programming errors. Additionally, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literal_(computer_programming)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Literal (computer programming)">literals</a> can and should be externalized into resource files/scripts where possible, to facilitate localization of software if it is intended to be deployed in different regions.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyclomatic_complexity" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Cyclomatic complexity">Cyclomatic complexity</a></i></b>: too many branches or loops; this may indicate a function needs to be broken up into smaller functions, or that it has potential for simplification.</li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downcasting" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Downcasting">Downcasting</a></i></b>: a type cast which breaks the abstraction model; the abstraction may have to be refactored or eliminated.<sup style="unicode-bidi: isolate; white-space: nowrap; font-size: 11.2px; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_smell#cite_note-7" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none; white-space: nowrap;">[7]</a></sup></li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><b><i>Orphan variable or constant class</i></b>: a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Class (computer science)">class</a> that typically has a collection of constants which belong elsewhere where those constants should be owned by one of the other member classes.</li></ul></li><li><div style="margin: 0.5em 0px; color: rgb(37, 37, 37); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><b>Method-level smells</b>:</div><ul style="list-style-type: disc; margin: 0.3em 0px 0px 1.6em; padding: 0px; list-style-image: url(data:image/svg+xml,%3C%3Fxml%20version%3D%221.0%22%20encoding%3D%22UTF-8%22%3F%3E%0A%3Csvg%20xmlns%3D%22http%3A%2F%2Fwww.w3.org%2F2000%2Fsvg%22%20version%3D%221.1%22%20width%3D%225%22%20height%3D%2213%22%3E%0A%3Ccircle%20cx%3D%222.5%22%20cy%3D%229.5%22%20r%3D%222.5%22%20fill%3D%22%2300528c%22%2F%3E%0A%3C%2Fsvg%3E%0A); font-family: sans-serif; font-size: 14px; font-style: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: start; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);"><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><b><i>Too many parameters</i></b>: a long list of parameters is hard to read, and makes calling and testing the function complicated. It may indicate that the purpose of the function is ill-conceived and that the code should be refactored so responsibility is assigned in a more clean-cut way.</span></li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><b><i>Long method</i></b>: a </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(computer_science)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Method (computer science)">method</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);">, function, or procedure that has grown too large.</span></li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><b><i>Excessively long identifiers</i></b>: in particular, the use of </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naming_convention_(programming)" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Naming convention (programming)">naming conventions</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"> to provide disambiguation that should be implicit in the </span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_architecture" style="text-decoration: none; color: rgb(11, 0, 128); background: none;" title="Software architecture">software architecture</a><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);">.</span></li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><b><i>Excessively short identifiers</i></b>: the name of a variable should reflect its function unless the function is obvious.</span></li><li style="margin-bottom: 0.1em;"><span style="color: rgb(37, 37, 37);"><b><i>Excessive return of data</i></b>: a function or method that returns more than what each of its callers needs.<br/><br/></span></li></ul></li></ul><hr/><div style="font-size: 24px;"><b>Data Structures</b></div><div><br/></div><div>String, Double, Boolean </div><div>Struct, Array, Key:Value</div><div>Python List = Array</div><div>Basic Array,</div><div>MultiDimensional Array () 2d 3d,</div><div>Jagged Array = Array of arrays - Declare child/nested array sizes.</div><div>     int[][] jaggedArray3 =</div><div>     {</div><div>         new int[] {1,3,5,7,9},</div><div>         new int[] {0,2,4,6},</div><div>         new int[] {11,22}</div><div>     };</div><div>Add, Create, Push</div><div>Move, Delete, Pop, Remove object at index</div><div>Access, Add, Delete, Find, Sort</div><div>Array: Resizing, Sort, Search</div><div>Linear - Brute Force - Binary: Divide and Conquer algorithm (Cannot be performed on unordered arrays)</div><hr/><div><div style="font-size: 24px;"><b>Programming Patterns</b></div><div><br/></div><div>Closed to modification, Open to extension.</div><div>What are subclasses? Superclasses?</div><div><br/></div><div>Class = Abstract object description. Can be part of a superclass, can contain subclasses. Becomes an object when <em>instantiated.</em></div><div>Method/member function = Allows an instantiated class or object to interact (think verbs) with other objects.</div><ul><li><strong>Strategy Pattern -</strong> <strong>In </strong><strong><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a></strong><strong>, the strategy pattern (also known as the policy pattern) is a </strong><strong><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design_pattern_(computer_science)">software design pattern</a></strong><strong> that enables an </strong><strong><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm">algorithm</a></strong><strong>'s behavior to be selected at runtime. The strategy pattern</strong><ul><li>defines a family of algorithms,</li><li>encapsulates each algorithm, and</li><li>makes the algorithms interchangeable within that family.</li></ul></li></ul><ul><li><strong>Decorator Pattern -</strong> In <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented programming</a>, the <strong>decorator pattern</strong> (also known as Wrapper, an alternative naming shared with the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adapter_pattern">Adapter pattern</a>) is a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design_pattern_(computer_science)">design pattern</a> that allows behavior to be added to an individual <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">object</a>, either statically or dynamically, without affecting the behavior of other objects from the same <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_(computer_science)">class</a>.<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decorator_pattern#cite_note-1">[1]</a></li></ul><ul><li><strong>Singleton Pattern</strong> - The singleton pattern is implemented by creating a class with a method that creates a new instance of the class if one does not exist. If an instance already exists, it simply returns a reference to that <strong>object</strong>. To make sure that the <strong>object</strong> cannot be instantiated any other way, the constructor is made private.</li></ul><ul><li><strong>Observer Pattern -</strong> The observer pattern is a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Design_pattern_(computer_science)">software design pattern</a> in which an <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)#Objects_in_object-oriented_programming">object</a>, called the subject, maintains a list of its dependents, called observers, and notifies them automatically of any state changes, usually by calling one of their <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Method_(computer_science)">methods</a>. It is mainly used to implement distributed <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Event_handling">event handling</a> systems. The Observer pattern is also a key part in the familiar <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Model%E2%80%93view%E2%80%93controller">model–view–controller</a> (MVC) architectural pattern.<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Observer_pattern#cite_note-jont-1">[1]</a> The observer pattern is implemented in numerous <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_library">programming libraries</a> and systems, including almost all <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GUI">GUI</a> toolkits.</li></ul><ul><li><strong>State Pattern -</strong> The <strong>state pattern</strong>, which closely resembles <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategy_pattern">Strategy Pattern</a>, is a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_pattern">behavioral</a> <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_design_pattern">software design pattern</a>, also known as the <strong>objects for states pattern</strong>. This pattern is used in <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a> to encapsulate varying behavior for the same routine based on an object's state <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computer_science)">object</a>. This can be a cleaner way for an object to change its behavior at runtime without resorting to large monolithic conditional statements<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_pattern#cite_note-GOF-1">[1]</a>:395.</li></ul><ul><li><strong>Combined Patterns (MVC)</strong></li></ul><div>Decorator Class</div><div>Concrete Class</div><div><br/></div><div>Thread Safety - A piece of code is <strong>thread</strong>-<strong>safe</strong> if it only manipulates shared data structures in a manner that guarantees <strong>safe</strong> execution by multiple <strong>threads</strong> at the same time. There are various strategies for making <strong>thread</strong>-<strong>safe</strong> data structures.</div><div><br/></div><div>In <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object-oriented_programming">object-oriented</a> <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, an <strong>iterator</strong> is an <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Object_(computing)">object</a> that enables a programmer to traverse a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Container_(data_structure)">container</a>, particularly <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_(abstract_data_type)">lists</a>.</div><div><br/></div><div>Single responsibility principle</div><div>Iterator responsibility principle</div><div><br/></div><div>Extending a class creates a sub class</div><div><br/></div></div><div>IDE - Integrated Development Environment</div><div><b><span style="font-size: 22px;"><span style="font-family: YogaAndroid, YogaLocal, Georgia, serif;"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17);"><br/></span></span></span></b></div><hr/><div><b><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); font-family: YogaAndroid, YogaLocal, Georgia, serif; font-size: 22px; font-style: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(26, 26, 26, 0.301961); -webkit-text-size-adjust: none; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; float: none; display: inline !important;">A Kubernetes cluster can be configured on mainstream Linux distributions, including CentOS, CoreOS, Debian, Fedora, Red Hat Linux and Ubuntu</span><br/></b></div><div><b><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); font-family: YogaAndroid, YogaLocal, Georgia, serif; font-size: 22px; font-style: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(26, 26, 26, 0.301961); -webkit-text-size-adjust: none; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; float: none; display: inline !important;"><br/></span></b></div><div><b><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); font-family: YogaAndroid, YogaLocal, Georgia, serif; font-size: 22px; font-style: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(26, 26, 26, 0.301961); -webkit-text-size-adjust: none; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; float: none; display: inline !important;"><span style="color: rgb(17, 17, 17); font-family: YogaAndroid, YogaLocal, Georgia, serif; font-size: 22px; font-style: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: auto; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: auto; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(26, 26, 26, 0.301961); -webkit-text-size-adjust: none; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">It can be deployed to run on local development machines; cloud platforms such as AWS, Azure and Google Cloud; virtualization environments based on KVM, vSphere and libvirt; and bare metal. Users can launch containers that run on Docker or rkt runtimes, and new container runtimes can be accommodated in the future.</span><br/></span></b></div><div><b><br/></b></div><hr/><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>Iaas</b></div><div>Infrastructure as a Service</div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>CaaS</b></div><div>Container as a Service</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Instana - Dynamic APM for Web-Scale Applications</b></div><div>Instana is the dynamic Application Performance Management solution that automatically monitors scaled modern applications and their quality of service.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Hyper-convergence (hyperconvergence)</b></div><div>is a type of infrastructure system with a software-centric architecture that tightly integrates compute, storage, networking and virtualization resources and other technologies from scratch in a commodity hardware box supported by a single vendor.</div><div><br/></div><hr/><div><br/></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Image.jpg" type="image/jpeg" style="height: auto;"/><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Image [12].png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">LDAP</b></div><div><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">(Lightweight Directory Access Protocol) is a software protocol for enabling anyone to locate organizations, individuals, and other resources such as files and devices in a network, whether on the public Internet or on a corporate intranet.</span></div><div><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">Business computer networks employ the </span><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">Lightweight Directory Access Protocol</b><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">, or </span><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">LDAP</b><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">, to distribute lists of information organized into hierarchies. To </span><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">access</b><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> a network's </span><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">LDAP</b><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> services, your computer must first </span><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">log</b><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;"> in to a server that supports the protocol, a process called </span><b style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255);">authentication</b><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34); font-family: arial, sans-serif; font-size: 16px; font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; orphans: 2; text-align: left; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; widows: 2; word-spacing: 0px; -webkit-text-stroke-width: 0px; background-color: rgb(255, 255, 255); display: inline !important; float: none;">.</span></div><div><b><br/></b></div><div><b>GITLAB CE</b></div><div>Tools for modern developers</div><div><br/></div><ul><li>GitLab unifies issues, code review, CI and CD into a single UI. Your tools make all the difference.</li><li>GitLab includes Git repository management, issue tracking, code review, an IDE, activity streams, wikis, and more. Shorten feedback cycles and increase confidence in your code.</li><li>GitLab has built-in CI and CD to test, build, and deploy your code. You can easily monitor the progress of your tests and build pipelines. Then deploy with the confidence that your code has been tested across multiple environments.</li><li>Cover your bases by adding control to your development process. With LDAP group sync, git hooks, automated testing, and audit trails, GitLab Enterprise Edition gives administrators user management capabilities without imposing on developers' workflows.</li></ul><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><br/></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Screen Shot 2015-06-20 at 2.32.08 PM.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/r3qcxzrd8kxyiissfj4f.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>FaaS</b></div><div>Functions as a Service</div><div><br/></div><div><b>BaaS</b></div><div>Backend as a Service</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>PostCSS</b></div><div>A tool for transforming CSS with JavaScript</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>SMAC</b></div><div>(social, mobile, analytics and cloud) is the concept that four technologies are currently driving business innovation. SMAC creates an ecosystem that allows a business to improve its operations and get closer to the customer with minimal overhead and maximum reach.</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>TDD</b></div><div>Test Driven Development</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>cURL</b></div><ul><li>is a computer software project providing a library and command-line tool for transferring data using various protocols. The cURL project produces two products, libcurl and cURL. It was first released in 1997. The name originally stood for &quot;see URL&quot;.</li><li>Since cURL uses libcurl, it supports a range of common Internet protocols, currently including HTTP, HTTPS, FTP, FTPS, SCP, SFTP, TFTP, LDAP, DAP, DICT, TELNET, FILE, IMAP, POP3, SMTP and RTSP (the last four only in versions newer than 7.20.0 or 9 February 2010).</li></ul><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div>While it is not a requirement for a front-end developer, knowing the connection on a TCP level is a nice thing to have, as is awareness of HTTP/2. Knowledge of REST services, at least from a consumer perspective, is certainly helpful as well.</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>A RESTful API</b></div><div>is an application program interface (API) that uses HTTP requests to GET, PUT, POST and DELETE data. Representational state transfer (REST), which is used by browsers, can be thought of as the language of the Internet.</div><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>ECMAScript</b></div><ul><li>To get ES6 working today, you need a JavaScript-to-JavaScript transpiler</li><li><a dir="ltr"></a><a dir="ltr"></a><a dir="ltr">Babel</a> (a transpiler) has a killer feature: human-readable output</li><li>Transpilers are here to stay</li><li>They allow you to compile code in the latest version into older versions of the language</li><li>As browser support gets better, we’ll transpile ES2016 and ES2017 into ES6 and beyond</li></ul><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>CSRF</b></div><div>Cross-site request forgery, also referred to as a ‘one-click attack’ or ‘session riding’ is a malicious exploit of a website in which unauthorized commands are sent from a user of a website that the victim trusts. The fundamental difference between CSRF and</div><div><br/></div><div><b>XSS</b></div><div>is that cross-site scripting (XSS),is designed to exploit the trust the user has for a particular site whilst CSRF aims to exploit the trust that a website has in the visitor’s browser. So, the key difference is within the victims browser.</div><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>NGINX</b></div><div>is a free, open-source, high-performance HTTP server and reverse proxy, as well as an IMAP/POP3 proxy server. NGINX is known for its high performance, stability, rich feature set, simple configuration, and low resource consumption.</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>Apache Mesos</b>: Data Center Operating Center</div><div><b>Mesosphere</b>: Data Center Operating System (DC/OS)</div><div><b>DC/OS</b>: Data Center Operating Center</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Kubernetes</b> vs. <b>Swarm</b> vs <b>Marathon</b> vs <b>Rancher</b>: Which <b>Container Orchestrator</b> is Best for You?</div><div><b>Apache Aurora</b> is a <b>Mesosphere</b> framework for long-running services and cron jobs.</div><div><b>Apache Chronos</b> is the “cron” for your <b>Mesosphere DC/OS</b>. It is a highly-available distributed job scheduler, providing the most robust way to run batch jobs in your datacenter. Chronos schedules jobs across the <b>Mesos</b> cluster and manages dependencies between jobs in an intelligent way.</div><div><b>Software-defined networking (SDN)</b></div><div>is an approach to computer networking that allows network administrators to manage network services through abstraction of lower-level functionality. SDN is meant to address the fact that the static architecture of traditional networks doesn't support the dynamic, scalable computing and storage needs of more modern computing environments such as data centers</div><div><b>Contrail</b>: Cloud networking and service orchestration powered by open technology.</div><div><b>Metronome</b>: Cron Service for DC/OS</div><div><b>Meteor</b>: Build Apps with JavaScript</div><div>Meteor is a complete platform for building web and mobile apps in pure JavaScript.</div><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>Omnibus</b></div><div>Easily create full-stack installers for your project across a variety of platforms.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>GitLab</b></div><div>Originally &quot;GitLab&quot; referred to a free repository manager. Today, this name can indicate:</div><div>- GitLab CE: the software, is a web-based Git repository manager with wiki and issue tracking features, using an open source licence.</div><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>Interactive Voice Response (IVR)</b></div><div>is an automated telephony system that interacts with callers, gathers information and routes calls to the appropriate recipient.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>VoiceXML (VXML)</b></div><div>is a digital document standard for specifying interactive media and voice dialogs between humans and computers. It is used for developing audio and voice response applications, such as banking systems and automated customer service portals.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Nuance Automatic Speech Recognition (ASR)</b></div><div>increases the efficiency of self-service applications and delivers an excellent customer experience – all with a flexible feature set and price point.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Genesys</b> is a company that sells customer experience and call center technology to mid-sized ...Genesys purchased IBM's CallPath computer telephony integration (CTI) assets in 2001.</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>In computing, Open Database Connectivity (ODBC)</b></div><div>is a standard application programming interface (API) for accessing database management systems (DBMS). The designers of ODBC aimed to make it independent of database systems and operating systems.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Java Database Connectivity (JDBC)</b></div><div>is an application programming interface (API) for the programming language Java, which defines how a client may access a database. It is part of the Java Standard Edition platform, from Oracle Corporation. It provides methods to query and update data in a database, and is oriented towards relational databases.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>PrimeFaces</b></div><div>is an open source user interface (UI) component library for <b>JavaServer Faces (JSF)</b> based applications, created by PrimeTek,[3] Turkey.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>JavaServer Faces (JSF)</b></div><div>is a Java specification for building component-based user interfaces for web applications.[1] It was formalized as a standard through the Java Community Process and is part of the Java Platform, Enterprise Edition.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Hibernate ORM</b></div><div>(Hibernate in short) is an object-relational mapping framework for the Java language. It provides a framework for mapping an object-oriented domain model to a relational database.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Object-relational mapping (ORM, O/RM, and O/R mapping tool)</b></div><div>in computer science is a programming technique for converting data between incompatible type systems in object-oriented programming languages. This creates, in effect, a &quot;virtual object database&quot; that can be used from within the programming language.\</div><div><br/></div><div><b>J2EE</b></div><div>is a platform-independent, Java-centric environment <a dir="ltr"></a><a dir="ltr"></a><a dir="ltr">from Sun</a> for developing, building and deploying Web-based enterprise applications online. The J2EE platform consists of a set of services, APIs, and protocols that provide the functionality for developing multitiered, Web-based applications.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Rational ClearCase</b></div><div>is a family of computer software tools that supports software configuration management (SCM) of source code and other software development assets. It also supports design-data management of electronic design artifacts, thus enabling hardware and software co-development.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>DB2</b></div><div>is a database product from IBM. It is a Relational Database Management System (RDBMS). DB2 is designed to store, analyze and retrieve the data efficiently. DB2product is extended with the support of Object-Oriented features and non-relational structures with XML.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>XSL</b></div><div>stands for EXtensible Stylesheet Language, and is a style sheet language for XML documents<b>.XSLT stands for XSL Transformations.</b></div><div><br/></div><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>A service-oriented architecture (SOA)</b></div><div>is a style of computer software where services are provided to the other components by application components, through acommunication protocol over a network. The basic fundamental principles of service oriented architecture is independent of vendors, products and technologies.[1] A service is a discrete unit of functionality that can be accessed remotely and acted upon and updated independently, such as an act of retrieving a credit card statement online.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Oracle WebLogic Server</b> is a <b>Java EE</b></div><div>application server currently developed by Oracle Corporation. Oracle acquired WebLogic Server when it purchased BEA Systems in 2008.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>UNIX System V</b></div><div>(pronounced: &quot;System Five&quot;) is one of the first commercial versions of the Unix operating system. It was originally developed by AT&amp;T and first released in 1983. Four major versions of System V were released, numbered 1, 2, 3, and 4. System V Release 4, or SVR4, was commercially the most successful version, being the result of an effort, marketed as &quot;Unix System Unification&quot;, which solicited the collaboration of the major Unix vendors. It was the source of several common commercial Unix features. System V is sometimes abbreviated to SysV.</div><div><br/></div><div>As of 2012, the Unix market is divided between three System V variants: IBM's AIX, Hewlett-Packard's HP-UX and Oracle's Solaris.[1]</div><div><br/></div><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>Red Hat Linux</b>, assembled by the company Red Hat, was a widely used Linux distribution until its discontinuation in 2004.[1]</div><div>Early releases of Red Hat Linux were called Red Hat Commercial Linux; Red Hat first published the software on November 3, 1994.[2] It was the first Linux distribution to use the RPM Package Manager as its packaging format, and over time has served as the starting point for several other distributions, such as Mandriva Linux and Yellow Dog Linux.</div><div>In 2003, Red Hat discontinued the Red Hat Linux line in favor of Red Hat Enterprise Linux (RHEL) for enterprise environments.Fedora, developed by the community-supported Fedora Project and sponsored by Red Hat, is a free-of-cost alternative intended for home use.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>RPM Package Manager (RPM)</b></div><div>(originally Red Hat Package Manager; now a recursive acronym) is a package management system. The name RPM refers to the following: the .rpm file format, files in the .rpm file format, software packaged in such files, and the package manager program itself.</div><div><br/></div><div><b>System integration testing (SIT)</b></div><div>involves the overall testing of a complete system of many subsystem components or elements. The system under test may be composed ofhardware, or software, or hardware with embedded software, or hardware/software with human-in-the-loop testing.</div><div>User acceptance testing (UAT) consists of a process of verifying that a solution works for the user.[6] It is not system testing (ensuring software does not crash and meets documented requirements), but rather ensures that the solution will work for the user (i.e., tests that the user accepts the solution); software vendors often refer to this as &quot;Beta testing&quot;.</div><div style="font-family:gotham, helvetica, arial, sans-serif;font-size:14px;"><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div>Tech to Research</div><div><span style="color: rgb(24, 24, 24);"><span style="font-family: Merriweather, Georgia, serif;"><b>Sorting algorithms</b></span></span></div><div><a href="https://www.toptal.com/developers/sorting-algorithms">https://www.toptal.com/developers/sorting-algorithms</a></div><div><br/></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Image.gif" 2017_files\en_todo [14].png"/>Yeoman</div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files\en_todo [15].png"/>Bower</div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/220px-Devops.svg.png" type="image/png"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>Useful Programming Concepts from Learning Java</b></div><div><br/></div><div>A static method or variable can be used without creating an insurance if it's class.</div><div>{} = a method or variables scope.</div><div><br/></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Evernote Camera Roll 20160218 142815.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Evernote Camera Roll 20160218 142815 [1].png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Evernote Camera Roll 20160215 155005.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Evernote Camera Roll 20160215 155006.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Evernote Camera Roll 20160211 155056.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>DevOps</b></div><div>is a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_development_methodology">software development method</a> that emphasizes <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communication">communication</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collaboration">collaboration</a> (information sharing and web service usage), <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/System_integration">integration</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automation">automation</a>, and measurement of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooperation">cooperation</a> between <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_developer">software developers</a> and other IT professionals.<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-1">[1]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-Erich_et_al-2">[2]</a> The method acknowledges the interdependence of software development,<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quality_assurance">quality assurance</a>, and IT operations, and aims to help an organization rapidly produce <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software">software</a> products and services and to improve operations performance.<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-Erich_et_al-2">[2]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-3">[3]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-4">[4]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-5">[5]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-mixing-6">[6]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-7">[7]</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DevOps#cite_note-8">[8]</a></div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div>400 Page is bad request</div><div>401 Page is unauthorized</div><div>403 Page is forbidden</div><div>404 Page not found</div><div>500 Internal Server Error</div><div><br/></div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>SOLID (object-oriented design)</b></div><div>In <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_programming">computer programming</a>, <b>SOLID</b> (<b>Single responsibility, Open-closed, Liskov substitution, Interface segregation and Dependency inversion</b>)</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><br/></div><div><b>POSIX</b> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English">/</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ˈ</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">p</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ɒ</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">z</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ɪ</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">k</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">s</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English">/</a> <i><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key">poz</a></b></i><i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key">-iks</a></i>), an acronym for &quot;<b>P</b>ortable <b>O</b>perating <b>S</b>ystem <b>I</b>nterface&quot;,<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX#cite_note-1">[1]</a> is a family of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standardization">standards</a> specified by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_of_Electrical_and_Electronics_Engineers">IEEE</a> for maintaining compatibility between <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operating_system">operating systems</a>. POSIX defines the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface">application programming interface</a> (API), along with command line <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_shell">shells</a> and utility interfaces, for software compatibility with variants of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix">Unix</a> and other operating systems.<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX#cite_note-FAQ-2">[2]</a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/POSIX#cite_note-IET-3">[3]</a></div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>Cygwin is:</b></div><ul><li>a large collection of GNU and Open Source tools which provide functionality similar to a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linux_distribution">Linux distribution</a> on Windows.</li></ul><div><b><br/></b></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><b>TeX</b></div><div>is a popular means by which to typeset complex <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_formulae">mathematical formulae</a>; it has been noted as one of the most sophisticated digital typographical systems in the world.<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TeX#cite_note-3">[3]</a> TeX is popular in <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academia">academia</a>, especially in<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics">mathematics</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science">computer science</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economics">economics</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engineering">engineering</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics">physics</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistics">statistics</a>, and <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantitative_psychology">quantitative psychology</a>. It has largely displaced <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix">Unix</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troff">troff</a>, the other favored formatter, in many Unix installations, which use both for different purposes. It is also used for many other typesetting tasks, especially in the form of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LaTeX">LaTeX</a>, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ConTeXt">ConTeXt</a>, and other template packages.</div><div><br/></div></div><hr/><div style="word-wrap: break-word; -webkit-nbsp-mode: space; -webkit-line-break: after-white-space;"><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files\en_todo [16].png"/><b>LaTeX</b> (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English">/</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ˈ</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">l</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ɑː</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">t</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ɛ</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">x</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English">/</a><i><b><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key">lah</a></b></i><i><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key">-tekh</a></i> or <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English">/</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ˈ</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">l</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">eɪ</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">t</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">ɛ</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key">x</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English">/</a><i><b><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key">lay</a></b></i><i><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Pronunciation_respelling_key">-tekh</a></i><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LaTeX#cite_note-1">[1]</a> shortening of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leslie_Lamport">Lamport</a><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TeX">TeX</a>) is a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_processor">document preparation system</a> and <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Document_markup_language">document markup language</a>. It is widely used for the communication and publication of scientific documents in many fields, including mathematics, physics, computer science, statistics, economics, and political science.<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LaTeX#cite_note-2">[2]</a></div><div><br/></div><div>Types of Testing</div><ul><li><b>Unit test</b>: Specify and test one point of the contract of single method of a class. This should have a very narrow and well defined scope. Complex dependencies and interactions to the outside world are<a href="http://martinfowler.com/articles/mocksArentStubs.html">stubbed or mocked</a>.</li><li><b>Integration test</b>: Test the correct inter-operation of multiple subsystems. There is whole spectrum there, from testing integration between two classes, to testing integration with the production environment.</li><li><b>Smoke test (aka Sanity check)</b>: A simple integration test where we just check that when the system under test is invoked it returns normally and does not blow up. It is an analogy with electronics, where the first test occurs when powering up a circuit: if it smokes, it's bad.</li><li><b>Regression test</b>: A test that was written when a bug was fixed. It ensure that this specific bug will not occur again. The full name is &quot;non-regression test&quot;. It can also be a test made prior to changing an application to make sure the application provides the same outcome.</li></ul><div>To this, I will add:</div><ul><li><b>Acceptance test</b>: Test that a feature or use case is correctly implemented. It is similar to an integration test, but with a focus on the use case to provide rather than on the components involved.</li><li><b>System test</b>: Test that tests a system as a black box. Dependencies on other systems are often mocked or stubbed during the test (otherwise it would be more of an integration test).</li><li><b>Pre-flight check</b>: Tests that are repeated in a production-like environment, to alleviate the 'builds on my machine' syndrome. Often this is realized by doing an acceptance or smoke test in a production like environment</li></ul><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/tddcycle.jpg" type="image/jpeg" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><i>comments are lies waiting to happen</i></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Capture [1].PNG" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div>MEAN = All JS Stack</div><div>Mongo Express Angular Node</div><div><br/></div><div><b>SCM</b></div><div><br/></div><div>Software Configuration Manger<br/></div><div><br/></div><div><b>Modernizr.js is a shim for HTML5 elements.</b></div><div><br/></div><div><i>YAML</i> is a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recursive_acronym">recursive acronym</a> for &quot;YAML Ain't <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markup_language">Markup Language</a>&quot;. Early in its development, <i>YAML</i> was said to mean &quot;<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yet_another">Yet Another</a> Markup Language&quot;,<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YAML#cite_note-YAML_spec_2001_08_01-3">[3]</a> but it was then reinterpreted (<a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backronym">backronyming</a> the original acronym) to distinguish its purpose as data-oriented, rather than document markup.<br/></div><div><br/></div><div><b>CLI Meaning</b></div><div><br/></div><div>A</div><div>command-line</div><div>interface (</div><div>CLI</div><div>), also known as</div><div>command-line</div><div>user interface, console user interface, and character user interface (CUI), is a means of interacting with a computer program where the user (or client) issues commands to the program in the form of successive lines of text (command lines).</div><div><br/></div><div><b>Asynchronous module definition</b> (<b>AMD</b>)</div><div><br/></div><div><a dir="ltr" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asynchronous_module_definition">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asynchronous_module_definition</a></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/220px-Asynchronous_Module_Definition_overview.png" type="image/png" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><br/></div><div>SO MANY BEST PRACTICES...</div><div><br/></div><div>combine and minify css and js</div><div>inline @imports</div><div>inline small images as data-uri</div><div>remove console.log</div><div>remove unused CSS</div><div>cache manifest creation</div><div>asset revving</div><div>dead code elimination</div><div>image compression</div><div>video/audio transcoding</div><div><br/></div><div>Illustrator Copy/Paste into Sublime Text === SVG wtf.</div><div>Can Export CSS from Illustrator</div><div>Device testing in Chrome Developer Tools now!</div><div>&quot;Single Responsibility Principle&quot;</div><div>Every Class should have a single responsibility, and that responsibility should be entirely encapsulated by the class.</div><div>Should be able to describe what it does without saying AND, OR</div><div><br/></div><div>Edge Reflow?</div><div>Great for responsive design</div><div>Edge Web fonts (google fonts competitor)</div><div><a href="https://edgewebfonts.adobe.com/fonts#/?collection=aladin">https://edgewebfonts.adobe.com/fonts#/?collection=aladin</a></div><div><br/></div><div>Node - Without a browser JS</div><div><b>Jade</b> - lightning fast Jade shorthand HTML.</div><div>How to modularize code to make testing easier/ unit testing</div><div>Precommit hooks</div><div><br/></div><div>JS Hint</div><div>w3schools is abhorrent, use Mozilla Developer Network, or</div><div>A good programmer is a lazy programmer; only lazy programmers will want to write the kind of tools that might replace them in the end. But for a lazy programmer to be a good programmer, he or she must be ncredibly unlazy when it comes to learning how to stay lazy.</div><div><br/></div><div>Browsers are the most volitile programming environment the world has ever known.</div><div>Browsers: UI&gt;Browsing Engine&gt;Render Engine&gt;Network,JS Engine,UI Backend</div><div>Main Flow: Parse HTML&gt;DOM Tree&gt;Render Tree&gt;Layout &amp; Paint</div><div>Requested by rendering engine in 8k chunks from the network layer</div><div>Parsing: Input&gt;lexical analysis&gt;syntax analysis&gt;output</div><div>Parsing HTML: Document&gt;tokenizer&gt;tree construction&gt;(Script Execution: document.write()-Back to tokenizer)&gt;DOM Tree</div><div>In <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lexical_analysis">lexical analysis</a>, <b>tokenization</b> is the process of breaking a stream of text up into words, phrases, symbols, or other meaningful elements called tokens.</div><div>Best Practice: Scripts at the bottom of the page.</div><div><br/></div><div>A <b>hash function</b> is any <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function">function</a> that can be used to map digital <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_(computing)">data</a> of arbitrary size to digital data of fixed size, with slight differences in input data producing very big differences in output data.</div><div>Bash = UNIX Shell</div><div>Browsers: Everything Except Network Operations Happens in a single thread.</div><div>XHR = XML HTTP Request</div><div><br/></div><div>IX Design =</div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Screen Shot 2015-01-08 at 5.27.20 PM.png" type="image/png"/><br/></div><div><br/></div><div><img src="_Programming Memorized  2017_files/Picture.jpeg" type="image/jpeg" style="height: auto;"/><br/></div></div></span>
